<span id="freeTextContainer8067461184121713400">Can You Keep a Secret is possibly my favorite Kinsella standalone.<br/><br/>It follows the story of Emma, an ordinary, slightly ditzy girl (think Anna from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss__Anna_and_the_French_Kiss___1_' title='Anna and the French Kiss (Anna and the French Kiss, #1) by Stephanie Perkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anna and the French Kiss</a>) who accidentally spills all her secrets to a stranger on the plane. And that stranger later turns out to be her boss. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409811061ra/11025861.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In honor of this book—and because I absolutely suck at writing reviews for books I love, I am going to spill to you, strangers of the Internet, <b>all of <i>my</i> secrets.</b> Okay, not all, but five.<br/><br/><b>1. I used to be majorly</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8067461184121713400" style="display:none">Can You Keep a Secret is possibly my favorite Kinsella standalone.<br><br>It follows the story of Emma, an ordinary, slightly ditzy girl (think Anna from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss__Anna_and_the_French_Kiss___1_" title="Anna and the French Kiss (Anna and the French Kiss, #1) by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a>) who accidentally spills all her secrets to a stranger on the plane. And that stranger later turns out to be her boss. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409811061ra/11025861.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In honor of this book—and because I absolutely suck at writing reviews for books I love, I am going to spill to you, strangers of the Internet, <b>all of <i>my</i> secrets.</b> Okay, not all, but five.<br><br><b>1. I used to be majorly obsessed with Seventeen magazine. </b> Back then, I begged my parents numerous times over the dinner table to buy me a subscription (all the savings!), but they always refused. In hindsight, that was probably a good thing because I soon got tired of all the high-definition pages of clothes, shoes, and make-up. The real sustenance was located in the back and only covered 4-5 pages. I'm proud to say that nowadays I blow my money on more worthy things, like badly-written YA novels that induce headaches.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409811061ra/11025862.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>2. <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405403480ra/10392727.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>That's a biggie.<br><br><b>3. I'm a huge fan of Taylor Swift, even though liking her is an extremely uncool thing these days.</b> Her lyrics are prose spun into music, that's all the reason I need.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409811061ra/11025863.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409811061ra/11025864.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409811107ra/11025868.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4. I sometimes think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19063.The_Book_Thief" title="The Book Thief by Markus Zusak" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Thief</a> is better than the Harry Potter series.</b> Then I make a pro-vs-con list in my head and all is right in the world once more.<br><br><b>5. I love Kinsella's work.</b> A lot of people hate them and I get it. Her heroines are essentially recycled book to book. The love interest is usually American and a logical businessman compared to the scatterbrained MC. They're filled with first-world problems and limited character growth. The problems work themselves out most of the time and the MC and Mr. Businessman go home happy and schmooze.<br><br>But at the same time, they're also <b>fun, compulsively readable, and keep me up reading til 2am</b> on a school night because I can't stop flipping the pages. They remind me that reading is indeed a hobby and something I look forward to after a long day, unlike <i>some</i> books I could mention *cough*<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7864437.The_Death_Cure__Maze_Runner___3_" title="The Death Cure (Maze Runner, #3) by James Dashner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Death Cure</a>*cough* <br><br>So the next time someone asks me who my favorite authors are, I'll say: "Stephen King, J. K Rowling, George R.R. Martin, Julie Kagawa, Markus Zusak, Meg Cabot, Sophie Kinsella—Yes, Sophie Kinsella."<br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer141099930292486379"><b>Worst book I have read in a LONG, long time. Seriously, How could so many of you like this book? </b>Now I remember why I hate chick-lit so much. After having read and adored <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42156.Something_Borrowed__Darcy___Rachel___1_' title='Something Borrowed (Darcy & Rachel, #1) by Emily Giffin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Something Borrowed</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42155.Something_Blue__Darcy___Rachel___2_' title='Something Blue (Darcy & Rachel, #2) by Emily Giffin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Something Blue</a> I thought I wasn't giving enough credit to this genre, I thought there were some good books on it out there.   <span id="freeText141099930292486379" style="display:none"><b>Worst book I have read in a LONG, long time. Seriously, How could so many of you like this book? </b>Now I remember why I hate chick-lit so much. After having read and adored <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42156.Something_Borrowed__Darcy___Rachel___1_" title="Something Borrowed (Darcy &amp; Rachel, #1) by Emily Giffin" rel="nofollow noopener">Something Borrowed</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42155.Something_Blue__Darcy___Rachel___2_" title="Something Blue (Darcy &amp; Rachel, #2) by Emily Giffin" rel="nofollow noopener">Something Blue</a> I thought I wasn't giving enough credit to this genre, I thought there were some good books on it out there. Because of this, I went to a list with the best chick-lit books and added them to my TBR pile. This is the first one I try and I completely abhorred it. <br /><br />I found this read and most of the characters absolutely shallow. The only character I did like was the Hero and we never really get to know him. The rest of the characters are vain, arrogant and egocentric. <b>Book's most discussed topics: Shoes, bags and celebrities.</b> OMG, I just can't believe there are so many books discussing these things. And I can't understand how someone can enjoy this type of reads. Seriously, if what you are looking for are funny, quick and entreating reads, you must search for contemporary romance. Just don't read more books in this genre... they can't be good for people's IQ. <br /><br />I just know there must be better books on this genre because those 2 I mentioned at the beginning of this review were great and I enjoyed them big time... I was expecting much more of everything form this book. I can't think of a thing I liked about it. I'll try another book of this author because I just can't believe everybody likes her so much and I enjoyed this book so little, maybe it was just the topic. </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1454295310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1726187393283619751">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Alright, I've been reading romance novels off late. It's one of those phases. And this is one of my favourites. Did Emma get on my nerves by whining too much? Sure. Was Jack way, way out of her league? Sure. But thing is, this woman knows how to pen chick-lit. She gets you right in the feelers and doesn't let go until you're sucked dry. <br/><br/>Emma, who I'm sure suffers from some form of anxiety, spills all her secrets to the gorgeous American sitting next to her. What transpires next is a ser</span>
  <span id="freeText1726187393283619751" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />Alright, I've been reading romance novels off late. It's one of those phases. And this is one of my favourites. Did Emma get on my nerves by whining too much? Sure. Was Jack way, way out of her league? Sure. But thing is, this woman knows how to pen chick-lit. She gets you right in the feelers and doesn't let go until you're sucked dry. <br /><br />Emma, who I'm sure suffers from some form of anxiety, spills all her secrets to the gorgeous American sitting next to her. What transpires next is a series of misadventures as she finds out he's none other than her boss. Like the boss man, boss; he owns the company she works for. Emma is your run of the mill, regular, working class girl. She takes the bus and hates her colleagues. She's a chronic underachiever, all thanks to her cousin Kerry. She loves her gramps, and is in one of those relationships. She has a best friend, she has a frenemy. And she has secrets. Lots of them. <br /><br />Jack on the other hand, oh Jack. He's smart, hot, and a little bit of an asshole. He kinda wears his heart on his sleeve, and fucks up majorly. But yeah, like every chick-lit books, they beat the odds together. Still, you know, this makes for a pleasing read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1726187393283619751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90268108?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90268108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12246101825601589332">Emma Corrigan is intolerably stupid. She lives with intolerably stupid flatmates, and has an intolerably stupid boyfriend whom she doesn't actually love but is determined to stay with because he is handsome.<br/><br/>Emma works for an intolerably stupid company (Panther Cola) and reports to tiny men with big egos that speak to her as though she is the biggest inconvenience in their day (my favourite lines are "Emma, please get your arse in gear" and "Emma, please get the <i>fuck</i> out of my office").<br/><br/>Instead of</span>
  <span id="freeText12246101825601589332" style="display:none">Emma Corrigan is intolerably stupid. She lives with intolerably stupid flatmates, and has an intolerably stupid boyfriend whom she doesn't actually love but is determined to stay with because he is handsome.<br /><br />Emma works for an intolerably stupid company (Panther Cola) and reports to tiny men with big egos that speak to her as though she is the biggest inconvenience in their day (my favourite lines are "Emma, please get your arse in gear" and "Emma, please get the <i>fuck</i> out of my office").<br /><br />Instead of handing in her notice as any self-respecting woman would and going to work in a more positive environment, Emma desperately seeks to move up the ladder so she can impress her intolerably stupid family who make fun of her because she isn't a CEO yet (she's only 25) by doing what's expected of her in her marketing assistant role and then pleading with her boss to promote her after one year even though she hasn't a clue in hell what she's doing.<br /><br />I've just reached the part where the CEO presses the emergency button in the elevator, thus trapping them inside together, and proceeds to tell her what kind of man she needs.<br /><br />No. Fucking. Thank you.</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_227443'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary"><img alt="Bridget Jones&#39;s Diary (Bridget Jones, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1558869586l/227443._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1X7+BuUYfp5R3kggG9mjYIuHX48mnVRB2Uan3ZLYP6XvWJfUXka39vb1/EHsLKm/Xdi4R+gQ2iaCOOFsX5vNPw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6160.Sophie_Kinsella">About Sophie Kinsella</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/6160.Sophie_Kinsella"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1245821549p3/6160.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/6160.Sophie_Kinsella">Sophie Kinsella
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
32,488
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14440866611319160302">Sophie Kinsella has sold over 40 million copies of her books in more than 60 countries, and she has been translated into over 40 languages.<br/><br/>Sophie Kinsella first hit the UK bestseller lists in September 2000 with her first novel in the Shopaholic series – The Secret Dreamworld of a Shopaholic (also published as Confessions of a Shopaholic). The book’s heroine, Becky Bloomwood – a fun and feisty fin</span>
  <span id="freeText14440866611319160302" style="display:none">Sophie Kinsella has sold over 40 million copies of her books in more than 60 countries, and she has been translated into over 40 languages.<br /><br />Sophie Kinsella first hit the UK bestseller lists in September 2000 with her first novel in the Shopaholic series – The Secret Dreamworld of a Shopaholic (also published as Confessions of a Shopaholic). The book’s heroine, Becky Bloomwood – a fun and feisty financial journalist who loves shopping but is hopeless with money – captured the hearts of readers worldwide. Becky has since featured in seven further bestselling books, Shopaholic Abroad (also published as Shopaholic Takes Manhattan), Shopaholic Ties the Knot, Shopaholic &amp; Sister, Shopaholic &amp; Baby, Mini Shopaholic, Shopaholic to the Stars and Shopaholic to the Rescue. Becky Bloomwood came to the big screen in 2009 with the hit Disney movie Confessions of a Shopaholic, starring Isla Fisher and Hugh Dancy.<br /><br />Sophie has also written seven standalone novels which have all been bestsellers in the UK, USA and other countries around the world: Can You Keep A Secret?, The Undomestic Goddess, Remember Me?, Twenties Girl, I’ve Got Your Number, Wedding Night, and My Not So Perfect Life, which was a Goodreads Choice Awards finalist for Best Fiction in 2017. <br /><br />In 2014 she published a Young Adult novel Finding Audrey about a teenage girl with social anxiety and her madcap family, and in January 2018, Sophie published her first illustrated book for young readers about the charming adventures of a mother-daughter fairy duo, Mummy Fairy and Me (also published as Fairy Mom and Me).<br /><br />Sophie’s latest novel, Surprise Me, published in February 2018, presents a humorous yet moving portrait of a marriage—its intricacies, comforts, and complications. Surprise Me reveals that hidden layers in a close relationship are often yet to be discovered.<br /><br />Sophie wrote her first novel under her real name, Madeleine Wickham, at the tender age of 24, whilst she was working as a financial journalist. The Tennis Party was immediately hailed as a success by critics and the public alike and became a top ten bestseller. She went on to publish six more novels as Madeleine Wickham: A Desirable Residence, Swimming Pool Sunday, The Gatecrasher, The Wedding Girl, Cocktails for Three and Sleeping Arrangements.<br /><br />Sophie was born in London. She studied music at New College, Oxford, but after a year switched to Politics, Philosophy and Economics. She now lives in London, UK, with her husband and family.<br /><br /><br />Visit Sophie's Facebook page: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/SophieKinsellaOfficial">http://www.facebook.com/SophieKinsell...</a><br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45600-shopaholic" rel="nofollow noopener">Shopaholic</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14440866611319160302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
